<p>The environmental impact of paper is significant, which has led to changes in industry and behaviour at both business and personal levels. With the use of modern technology such as the <a href="/wiki/Printing_press" title="Printing press">printing press</a> and the highly mechanised harvesting of wood, paper has become a cheap commodity. This has led to a high level of consumption and waste. With the rise in environmental awareness due to the lobbying by <a href="/wiki/Environmental_organization" title="Environmental organization">environmental organizations</a> and with increased government regulation there is now a trend towards <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Pulp_and_paper_industry" title="Pulp and paper industry">pulp and paper industry</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Plastics">Plastics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Plastics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Plastic#Environmental_effects" title="Plastic">Plastic § Environmental effects</a></div>
<p>Some scientists suggest that by 2050 there could be more plastic than fish in the oceans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pesticides">Pesticides</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Pesticides">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_pesticides" title="Environmental impact of pesticides">Environmental impact of pesticides</a></div>
<p>The environmental impact of <a href="/wiki/Pesticide" title="Pesticide">pesticides</a> is often greater than what is intended by those who use them. Over 98% of sprayed insecticides and 95% of herbicides reach a destination other than their target species, including nontarget species, air, water, bottom sediments, and food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sustaining_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-sustaining-100">[100]</a></sup> Pesticide contaminates land and water when it escapes from production sites and storage tanks, when it runs off from fields, when it is discarded, when it is sprayed aerially, and when it is sprayed into water to kill algae.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tashkent_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tashkent-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p>The amount of pesticide that migrates from the intended application area is influenced by the particular chemical's properties: its propensity for binding to soil, its <a href="/wiki/Vapor_pressure" title="Vapor pressure">vapor pressure</a>, its water <a href="/wiki/Solubility" title="Solubility">solubility</a>, and its resistance to being broken down over time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kelloggrl_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kelloggrl-102">[102]</a></sup> Factors in the soil, such as its texture, its ability to retain water, and the amount of organic matter contained in it, also affect the amount of pesticide that will leave the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kelloggrl_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kelloggrl-102">[102]</a></sup> Some pesticides contribute to <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> and the depletion of the <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">ozone layer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reynoldsjd_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-reynoldsjd-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pharmaceuticals_and_personal_care_products">Pharmaceuticals and personal care products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Pharmaceuticals and personal care products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_pharmaceuticals_and_personal_care_products" title="Environmental impact of pharmaceuticals and personal care products">Environmental impact of pharmaceuticals and personal care products</a></div>
<p>The environmental impact of pharmaceuticals and personal care products (PPCPs) is largely speculative. PPCPs are substances used by individuals for personal health or <a href="/wiki/Cosmetics" title="Cosmetics">cosmetic</a> reasons and the products used by <a href="/wiki/Agribusiness" title="Agribusiness">agribusiness</a> to boost growth or health of livestock. PPCPs have been detected in water bodies throughout the world. The effects of these chemicals on humans and the environment are not yet known, but to date there is no scientific evidence that they affect human health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epa_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-epa-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_mining" title="Environmental impact of mining">Environmental impact of mining</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="488" data-file-width="650" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg/220px-Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg/330px-Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg/440px-Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Acid mine drainage in the Rio Tinto River</div></div></div>
<p>The environmental impact of mining includes <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a>, formation of <a href="/wiki/Sinkhole" title="Sinkhole">sinkholes</a>, loss of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>, and contamination of soil, <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">groundwater</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surface_water" title="Surface water">surface water</a> by chemicals from mining processes. In some cases, additional forest logging is done in the vicinity of mines to increase the available room for the storage of the created debris and soil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Besides creating environmental damage, the contamination resulting from leakage of chemicals also affect the health of the local population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Mining companies in some countries are required to follow environmental and rehabilitation codes, ensuring the area mined is returned to close to its original state. Some mining methods may have significant environmental and public health effects.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_transport" title="Environmental impact of transport">Environmental impact of transport</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:45intoI-10_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/45intoI-10_2.jpg/220px-45intoI-10_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/45intoI-10_2.jpg/330px-45intoI-10_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/45intoI-10_2.jpg/440px-45intoI-10_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:45intoI-10_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_10_(Texas)" title="Interstate 10 (Texas)">Interstate 10</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_45_(Texas)" title="Interstate 45 (Texas)">Interstate 45</a> near downtown <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> in the United States</div></div></div>
<p>The environmental impact of <a href="/wiki/Transport" title="Transport">transport</a> is significant because it is a major user of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_and_society" title="Energy and society">energy</a>, and burns most of the world's <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>. This creates <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Nitrous_oxide" title="Nitrous oxide">nitrous oxides</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Particulate" title="Particulate">particulates</a>, and is a significant contributor to <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> through emission of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pnas_pdf_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-pnas_pdf-107">[107]</a></sup> for which transport is the fastest-growing emission sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> By subsector, road transport is the largest contributor to global warming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pnas_pdf_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-pnas_pdf-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_regulation" title="Environmental regulation">Environmental regulations</a> in developed countries have reduced the individual vehicles emission; however, this has been offset by an increase in the number of vehicles, and more use of each vehicle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pnas_pdf_107-2"><a href="#cite_note-pnas_pdf-107">[107]</a></sup> Some pathways to reduce the carbon emissions of road vehicles considerably have been studied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Energy use and emissions vary largely between modes, causing <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalists</a> to call for a transition from air and road to rail and human-powered transport, and increase <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transport_electrification" title="Transport electrification">transport electrification</a> and <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a>.
</p><p>Other environmental impacts of transport systems include <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">traffic congestion</a> and automobile-oriented <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a>, which can consume natural habitat and agricultural lands. By reducing transportation emissions globally, it is predicted that there will be significant positive effects on Earth's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_quality" title="Air quality">air quality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acid_rain" title="Acid rain">acid rain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smog" title="Smog">smog</a> and climate change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p><p>The health impact of transport emissions is also of concern. A recent survey of the studies on the effect of traffic emissions on pregnancy outcomes has linked exposure to emissions to adverse effects on gestational duration and possibly also intrauterine growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aviation">Aviation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Aviation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_aviation" title="Environmental impact of aviation">Environmental impact of aviation</a></div>
<p>The environmental impact of aviation occurs because <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_engine" title="Aircraft engine">aircraft engines</a> emit <a href="/wiki/Noise_pollution" title="Noise pollution">noise</a>, particulates, and gases which contribute to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICAO_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-ICAO-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Enviro.aeroImpact_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Enviro.aeroImpact-113">[113]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Global_dimming" title="Global dimming">global dimming</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-contrails_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-contrails-114">[114]</a></sup> Despite emission reductions from automobiles and more fuel-efficient and less polluting <a href="/wiki/Turbofan" title="Turbofan">turbofan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turboprop" title="Turboprop">turboprop</a> engines, the rapid growth of <a href="/wiki/Air_travel" title="Air travel">air travel</a> in recent years contributes to an increase in total pollution attributable to <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">aviation</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions from aviation increased by 87% between 1990 and 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Among <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_aviation#Reducing_air_travel" title="Environmental impact of aviation">other factors</a> leading to this phenomenon are the increasing number of <a href="/wiki/Hypermobility_(travel)" title="Hypermobility (travel)">hypermobile travellers</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gossling_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-gossling-116">[116]</a></sup> and social factors that are making air travel commonplace, such as <a href="/wiki/Frequent-flyer_program#Climate_and_environmental_issues" title="Frequent-flyer program">frequent flyer programs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gossling_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-gossling-116">[116]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is an ongoing debate about possible <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taxation" title="Taxation">taxation</a> of air travel and the inclusion of aviation in an <a href="/wiki/Emissions_trading" title="Emissions trading">emissions trading</a> scheme, with a view to ensuring that the total <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/External_costs" title="External costs">external costs</a> of aviation are taken into account.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_roads" title="Environmental impact of roads">Environmental impact of roads</a></div>
<p>The environmental impact of roads includes the local effects of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highways" title="Highways">highways</a> (public <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roads" title="Roads">roads</a>) such as on noise, <a href="/wiki/Light_pollution" title="Light pollution">light pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">water pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">habitat destruction</a>/disturbance and local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_quality" title="Air quality">air quality</a>; and the wider effects including <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> from vehicle emissions. The design, construction and management of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roads" title="Roads">roads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parking" title="Parking">parking</a> and other related facilities as well as the design and regulation of <a href="/wiki/Vehicle" title="Vehicle">vehicles</a> can change the impacts to varying degrees.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Shipping">Shipping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Shipping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_shipping" title="Environmental impact of shipping">Environmental impact of shipping</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1293" data-file-width="1800" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg/220px-%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg/330px-%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg/440px-%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Agent_Orange" title="Agent Orange">Agent Orange</a> spray run by aircraft, part of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Ranch_Hand" title="Operation Ranch Hand">Operation Ranch Hand</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The environmental impact of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shipping" title="Shipping">shipping</a> includes <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_pollution" title="Oil pollution">oil pollution</a>. In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> emissions from shipping were estimated at 4 to 5% of the global total, and estimated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Maritime_Organisation" title="International Maritime Organisation">International Maritime Organisation</a> (IMO) to rise by up to 72% by 2020 if no action is taken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> There is also a potential for introducing invasive species into new areas through shipping, usually by attaching themselves to the ship's hull.
</p><p>The First Intersessional Meeting of the IMO Working Group on Greenhouse Gas Emissions<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> from Ships took place in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> on 23–27 June 2008. It was tasked with developing the technical basis for the reduction mechanisms that may form part of a future IMO regime to control greenhouse gas emissions from international shipping, and a draft of the actual reduction mechanisms themselves, for further consideration by IMO’s Marine Environment Protection Committee (MEPC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>General military spending and military activities have marked environmental effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-121">[121]</a></sup> The United States military is considered one of the worst polluters in the world, responsible for over 39,000 sites contaminated with hazardous materials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Several studies have also found a strong positive correlation between higher military spending and higher <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">carbon emissions</a> where increased military spending has a larger effect on increasing carbon emissions in the Global North than in the Global South.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-121">[121]</a></sup> Military activities also affect land use and are extremely resource-intensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup>
</p><p>The military does not solely have negative effects on the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> There are several examples of militaries aiding in land management, conservation, and greening of an area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Additionally, certain military technologies have proven extremely helpful for conservationists and environmental scientists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War">War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_war" title="Environmental impact of war">Environmental impact of war</a></div>
<p>As well as the cost to human life and society, there is a significant environmental impact of war. <a href="/wiki/Scorched_earth" title="Scorched earth">Scorched earth</a> methods during, or after war have been in use for much of recorded history but with modern <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a> war can cause a far greater devastation on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)" title="Environment (biophysical)">environment</a>. <a href="/wiki/Unexploded_ordnance" title="Unexploded ordnance">Unexploded ordnance</a> can render land unusable for further use or make access across it dangerous or fatal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_degradation_effects">Environmental degradation effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Environmental degradation effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_degradation" title="Environmental degradation">Environmental degradation</a></div>
<p>Human activity is causing <a href="/wiki/Environmental_degradation" title="Environmental degradation">environmental degradation</a>, which is the deterioration of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)" title="Environment (biophysical)">environment</a> through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Depletion_of_resources" title="Depletion of resources">depletion of resources</a> such as air, water and soil; the destruction of ecosystems; <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">habitat destruction</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a> of wildlife; and <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a>. It is defined as any change or disturbance to the environment perceived to be deleterious or undesirable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> As indicated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I%3DPAT" title="I=PAT">I=PAT</a> equation, environmental impact (I) or degradation is caused by the combination of an already very large and increasing human population (P), continually increasing <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a> or per capita affluence (A), and the application of resource-depleting and polluting technology (T).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Mass_extinction.2C_defaunation.2C_and_decline_in_biodiversity"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_extinction,_defaunation,_and_decline_in_biodiversity">Mass extinction, defaunation, and decline in biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Mass extinction, defaunation, and decline in biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Holocene_extinction" title="Holocene extinction">Holocene extinction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Defaunation" title="Defaunation">Defaunation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_loss" title="Biodiversity loss">Biodiversity loss</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ecological_collapse" title="Ecological collapse">Ecological collapse</a></div>
<p>Biodiversity generally refers to the variety and variability of life on Earth, and is represented by the number of different species there are on the planet. Since its introduction, Homo sapiens (the human species) has been killing off entire species either directly (such as through hunting) or indirectly (such as by <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">destroying habitats</a>), causing the <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a> of species at an alarming rate. Humans are the cause of the current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass_extinction" title="Mass extinction">mass extinction</a>, called the <a href="/wiki/Holocene_extinction" title="Holocene extinction">Holocene extinction</a>, driving extinctions to 100 to 1000 times the normal background rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Though most experts agree that human beings have accelerated the rate of species extinction, some scholars have postulated without humans, the biodiversity of the Earth would grow at an exponential rate rather than decline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SahneyBentonFerry2010LinksDiversityVertebrates_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-SahneyBentonFerry2010LinksDiversityVertebrates-2">[2]</a></sup> The Holocene extinction continues, with <a href="/wiki/Meat#Environmental_impact" title="Meat">meat consumption</a>, <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">overfishing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">ocean acidification</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Decline_in_amphibian_populations" title="Decline in amphibian populations">amphibian crisis</a> being a few broader examples of an almost universal, <a href="/wiki/Cosmopolitan_distribution" title="Cosmopolitan distribution">cosmopolitan</a> decline in biodiversity. <a href="/wiki/Human_overpopulation" title="Human overpopulation">Human overpopulation</a> (and continued <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_population_growth" title="Human population growth">population growth</a>) along with <a href="/wiki/Overconsumption" title="Overconsumption">profligate consumption</a> are considered to be the primary drivers of this rapid decline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ceballos-Ehrlich-2017-05_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ceballos-Ehrlich-2017-05-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PimmJenkins_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-PimmJenkins-135">[135]</a></sup> A 2017 statement by 15,364 scientists from 184 countries warned that, among other things, this sixth extinction event unleashed by humanity could annihilate many current life forms and consign them to extinction by the end of this century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldScientists_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-WorldScientists-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Defaunation" title="Defaunation">Defaunation</a> is the loss of animals from ecological communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-def_ant_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-def_ant-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p><p>It is estimated that more than 50 percent of all wildlife has been lost in the last 40 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> It is estimated that by 2020, 68% of the world's wildlife will be lost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, there is believed to be a 70 percent loss.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> A May 2018 study published in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PNAS" title="PNAS">PNAS</a></i> found that 83% of wild mammals, 80% of marine mammals, 50% of plants and 15% of fish have been lost since the dawn of human civilization. Currently, livestock make up 60% of all mammals on earth, followed by humans (36%) and wild mammals (4%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-loss_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-loss-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_coral_reefs">Death of coral reefs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Death of coral reefs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_impact_on_coral_reefs" title="Human impact on coral reefs">Human impact on coral reefs</a></div>
<p>Because of human overpopulation, <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> are dying around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coral_reefs_around_the_world_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coral_reefs_around_the_world-140">[140]</a></sup> In particular, coral mining, <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a> (organic and non-organic), <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">overfishing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blast_fishing" title="Blast fishing">blast fishing</a> and the digging of <a href="/wiki/Canal" title="Canal">canals</a> and access into islands and bays are serious threats to these ecosystems. Coral reefs also face high dangers from pollution, diseases, destructive fishing practices and warming oceans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tough_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-tough-141">[141]</a></sup> In order to find answers for these problems, researchers study the various factors that impact reefs. The list of factors is long, including the ocean's role as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_sink" title="Carbon dioxide sink">carbon dioxide sink</a>, atmospheric changes, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultraviolet_light" title="Ultraviolet light">ultraviolet light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">ocean acidification</a>, biological <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">virus</a>, impacts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dust_storms" title="Dust storms">dust storms</a> carrying agents to far flung reefs, pollutants, <a href="/wiki/Algal_bloom" title="Algal bloom">algal blooms</a> and others. Reefs are threatened well beyond coastal areas.
</p><p>General estimates show approximately 10% world's coral reefs are already dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kleypas,_J.A._2006_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kleypas,_J.A._2006-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> It is estimated that about 60% of the world's reefs are at risk due to destructive, human-related activities. The threat to the health of reefs is particularly strong in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, where 80% of reefs are <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline_in_amphibian_populations">Decline in amphibian populations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Decline in amphibian populations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Decline_in_amphibian_populations" title="Decline in amphibian populations">Decline in amphibian populations</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_warming">Global warming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Global warming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">Global warming</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Runaway_climate_change" title="Runaway climate change">Runaway climate change</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">Global warming</a> is the result of increasing atmospheric carbon dioxide concentrations which is caused primarily by the combustion of fossil energy sources such as petroleum, coal, and natural gas, and to an unknown extent by destruction of forests, increased methane, volcanic activity and cement production. Such massive alteration of the global carbon cycle has only been possible because of the availability and deployment of advanced technologies, ranging in application from fossil fuel exploration, extraction, distribution, refining, and combustion in power plants and automobile engines and advanced farming practices. Livestock contributes to climate change both through the production of greenhouse gases and through destruction of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_sink" title="Carbon sink">carbon sinks</a> such as rain-forests. According to the 2006 United Nations/FAO report, 18% of all greenhouse gas emissions found in the atmosphere are due to livestock. The raising of livestock and the land needed to feed them has resulted in the destruction millions of acres of Rainforest and as global demand for meat rises, so too will the demand for land. Ninety-one percent of all rainforest land deforested since 1970 is now used for livestock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Potential negative environmental impacts caused by increasing atmospheric carbon dioxide concentrations are rising global air temperatures, altered hydrogeological cycles resulting in more frequent and severe droughts, storms, and floods, as well as sea level rise and ecosystem disruption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPCC_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC-146">[146]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Habitat_destruction">Habitat destruction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Habitat destruction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">Habitat destruction</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_degradation">Land degradation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Land degradation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Land_degradation" title="Land degradation">Land degradation</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Land_degradation" title="Land degradation">Land degradation</a> is a process in which the value of the <a href="/wiki/Biophysical_environment" title="Biophysical environment">biophysical environment</a> is affected by a combination of human-induced processes acting upon the land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rural_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-rural-147">[147]</a></sup> It is viewed as any change or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecological_disturbance" title="Ecological disturbance">disturbance</a> to the land perceived to be deleterious or undesirable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Natural_hazard" title="Natural hazard">Natural hazards</a> are excluded as a cause; however human activities can indirectly affect phenomena such as floods and bush fires.
</p><p>This is considered to be an important topic of the <a href="/wiki/21st_century" title="21st century">21st century</a> due to the implications land degradation has upon <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agronomic_productivity" title="Agronomic productivity">agronomic productivity</a>, the environment, and its effects on <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> It is estimated that up to 40% of the world's agricultural land is seriously degraded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Desertification">Desertification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Desertification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">Desertification</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ocean_acidification">Ocean acidification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Ocean acidification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">Ocean acidification</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ozone_depletion">Ozone depletion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Ozone depletion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ozone_depletion" title="Ozone depletion">Ozone depletion</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_degradation">Water degradation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Water degradation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_degradation" title="Water degradation">Water degradation</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disruption_of_the_nitrogen_cycle">Disruption of the nitrogen cycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Disruption of the nitrogen cycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_impact_on_the_nitrogen_cycle" title="Human impact on the nitrogen cycle">Human impact on the nitrogen cycle</a></div>
<p>Of particular concern is N<sub>2</sub>O, which has an average atmospheric lifetime of 114–120 years,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> and is 300 times more effective than CO<sub>2</sub> as a <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schles_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schles-152">[152]</a></sup> NO<sub>x</sub> produced by industrial processes, automobiles and agricultural fertilization and NH<sub>3</sub> emitted from soils (i.e., as an additional byproduct of nitrification)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schles_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-Schles-152">[152]</a></sup> and livestock operations are transported to downwind ecosystems, influencing N cycling and nutrient losses. Six major effects of NO<sub>x</sub> and NH<sub>3</sub> emissions have been identified:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gallo2003_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-gallo2003-153">[153]</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>decreased atmospheric visibility due to ammonium aerosols (fine <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_particulate_matter" title="Atmospheric particulate matter">particulate matter</a> [PM])</li>
<li>elevated <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a> concentrations</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a> and PM affects human health (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_disease" title="Respiratory disease">respiratory diseases</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>)</li>
<li>increases in <a href="/wiki/Radiative_forcing" title="Radiative forcing">radiative forcing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a></li>
<li>decreased agricultural productivity due to <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a> deposition</li>
<li>ecosystem acidification<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-houdijk_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-houdijk-154">[154]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Eutrophication" title="Eutrophication">eutrophication</a>.</li></ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_human_health">Effects on human health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Effects on human health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Human impacts upon the environment, such as pollution and global warming, in turn affect human health.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_of_global_warming_on_human_health">Effects of global warming on human health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Effects of global warming on human health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

U.S. Global Change Research Program. <q>This assessment concludes, based on extensive evidence, that it is extremely likely that human activities, especially emissions of greenhouse gases, are the dominant cause of the observed warming since the mid-20th century. For the warming over the last century, there is no convincing alternative explanation supported by the extent of the observational evidence. In addition to warming, many other aspects of global climate are changing, primarily in response to human activities. Thousands of studies conducted by researchers around the world have documented changes in surface, atmospheric, and oceanic temperatures; melting glaciers; diminishing snow cover; shrinking sea ice; rising sea levels; ocean acidification; and increasing atmospheric water vapor.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" <li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="https://www3.epa.gov/climatechange//kids/impacts/signs/acidity.html" rel="nofollow">"Increased Ocean Acidity"</a>. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epa.gov" title="Epa.gov">epa.gov</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">United States Environmental Protection Agency</a>. 30 August 2016<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">23 November</span> 2017</span>. <q>Carbon dioxide is added to the atmosphere whenever people burn fossil fuels. Oceans play an important role in keeping the Earth's carbon cycle in balance. As the amount of carbon dioxide in the atmosphere rises, the oceans absorb a lot of it. In the ocean, carbon dioxide reacts with seawater to form carbonic acid. This causes the acidity of seawater to increase.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=epa.gov&amp;rft.atitle=Increased+Ocean+Acidity&amp;rft.date=2016-08-30&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww3.epa.gov%2Fclimatechange%2F%2Fkids%2Fimpacts%2Fsigns%2Facidity.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+impact+on+the+environment"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Ceballos-Ehrlich-2017-05-134"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Ceballos-Ehrlich-2017-05_134-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Ceballos, Gerardo; Ehrlich, Paul R; Dirzo, Rodolfo (23 May 2017). <a class="external text" href="http://www.pnas.org/content/early/2017/07/05/1704949114.full" rel="nofollow">"Biological annihilation via the ongoing sixth mass extinction signaled by vertebrate population losses and declines"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Proceedings_of_the_National_Academy_of_Sciences_of_the_United_States_of_America" title="Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences of the United States of America">PNAS</a></i>. <b>114</b> (30): E6089–E6096. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1073%2Fpnas.1704949114" rel="nofollow">10.1073/pnas.1704949114</a>. <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Central" title="PubMed Central">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5544311" rel="nofollow">5544311</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/28696295" rel="nofollow">28696295</a>. <q>Much less frequently mentioned are, however, the ultimate drivers of those immediate causes of biotic destruction, namely, human overpopulation and continued population growth, and overconsumption, especially by the rich. These drivers, all of which trace to the fiction that perpetual growth can occur on a finite planet, are themselves increasing rapidly.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=PNAS&amp;rft.atitle=Biological+annihilation+via+the+ongoing+sixth+mass+extinction+signaled+by+vertebrate+population+losses+and+declines&amp;rft.volume=114&amp;rft.issue=30&amp;rft.pages=E6089-E6096&amp;rft.date=2017-05-23&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5544311&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F28696295&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1073%2Fpnas.1704949114&amp;rft.aulast=Ceballos&amp;rft.aufirst=Gerardo&amp;rft.au=Ehrlich%2C+Paul+R&amp;rft.au=Dirzo%2C+Rodolfo&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.pnas.org%2Fcontent%2Fearly%2F2017%2F07%2F05%2F1704949114.full&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+impact+on+the+environment"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>
